<Date>1610291764126<//Date><UserId.>116844923292442215681<//UserId.><Rate>5</Rate>< text>
Gorgeous views and a wonderful place to take a walk/hike, you can make the walk harder by taking the side hills and getting more vertical distance.. from the start of the trail to the park it is 3.9 miles and 666' of vertical elevation gain..
Always keep an eye out as there are some gorgeous places to take pictures..</text>

<date>1606625192658<//date><pictures>None< /pictures><user_id>106357010500504077223< /user_id><gmap_id>0x80c2987380a53efd:0x9e460d18602e2aad<//gmap_id><user_name>Michael Kovac<//user_name><review>How did I not know about this excellent, easy to access, in town hike? In the heart of Mulholland, this hike provides everything from an easy unpaved road hike with great views to a bit of history at the topic (with 360 degrees of epic city views). With decent street parking at the bottom of the hill, you'll find a comfortable walk for even the most hike averse - and end up at a former Nike Missile Control Tower overlooking the Valley. Fun for families and everyone - and really interesting to see this Cold War relic replete with detailed signage on what happened on the site in the 1950-60s.<//review><resp>None<//resp><rate>5<//rate></record></dataset><record>

Just to start the entrance to this park  is not from Mulholland drive but the other side. One must drive on sunset BLVD and take a right 5 miles up. Google maps gave me the wrong direction because the road was blocked.

<user_name>Dawn Martin</user_name>< Review>
Difficulty: Med to Low
Parking: Sufficient
Dogs: Allowed on Leash

Vox and I went to check out this park and arrived at 7.50am on a Sunday morning.  The parking in the little parking area was already totally packed but we got 1 of two spots left.  I was surprised to see so many people there so early!

We took the hike up to the Nike Missile area and then checked that out.  When we were done we continued following the trail for another .5 miles or so.  i have no idea where it ends!

The .8 miles are all up hill to the Nike area but it's not too hard.  If you're not an athelete and are semi-out of shape you'll find it a fun challenge.

There are other trails there that we didn't take.  I'm already planning when to go back and try out more trails.</Review>

<gmap_id>0x80dd2bea4865669b:0xf68dd64dbfe9db69< /gmap_id><user_name>Ada Bates</user_name>< review>
I'd stopped into the shop a few days ago to grab a menu--I'd seen it on line, but one place said they didn't do take out, so I wanted to make sure. They do.

Yesterday, my husband went in to pick up lunch: kalbi ribs and wagyu beef plates with rice, kale salad, and a cabbage slaw with thin-sliced avocado on top.

Every bite was amazing! Tender, flavorful meats with delicious sauces, fresh and crispy salads with vibrant dressings--that are perfect accompaniments to the meat.

The plates were presented beautifully and weren't dripping sauce or grease (I hate sloppy to-go containers). It was very clear these guys care about the food and how they present it to customers!

It's a lovely little shop with friendly and informative staff, and it would be pleasant to dine in, when we can.

I highly recommend ordering from this gem!< /review>

<rating>5</rating>< Text>
Buena Park, Calif (Orange County)

One of the best spots for chicken bowl type of eatings.

Service: Pleasant.

Food: OMG the chicken and wagyu beef is surreal.
Chicken: Typical fire grilled teriyaki. Bit salty for me and goes well with the house teri sauce & hot sauce.
Beef: Drool. Quality, softness and flavor is on point. Best beef bowl in America.
Mac Salad: For a $1 or $2 depending on size is worth it. I typically grab double mac. Whoever makes this for them deserves a cookie, pat in the back and a high five. It's commercialized/processed, but, not too obvious.
Rice: Korean style. Sticky. Preferred rice.
Salad: Sucks... Cause who raves about a damn salad?

Location: SE Plaza on Orangethorpe/Beach. Heavy congestion especially around Halloween. Adjacent to Fuddruckers.

Decor/Interior: Small. Limited seating.

Cost: $10ish. Appx $16 for legit fatties.

My favorite lunch spot =)
Happy eatings.
@cigarcpa< /Text>

Recently i went and it might have been the day/time but  there was mostly a lot of young adults/teens and a lot of them were blasting innapropriate music, acting like they own the place and leaving trash everywhere. Went at 10:45am on a Saturday, not knowing there was a designated time for kids to swim, which was noon. I see a family (mother, father, baby) playing and splashing in the water. When I pointed this out to the girl at the counter I asked why they were allowed in while my family wasn't. Her exact response was "They have special permission from my higher up". So it's nice to know someone that works here I guess. I had to explain to my children that those people were getting special treatment, and we weren't allowed in. <Rating>5<//Rating><Resp>None< /Resp>< Review>
Whether you're a resident Los Angelo or a visitor to the City of Angels, the French Florist should be your "go-to" place should you desire vibrant, custom designed floral arrangements that are second to none in the design genre.

The owner's, Steve and Angela, along with their talented troop of designers and ever multi-tasking diligent staff are always, or so it seems, going far and above the call to surpass the expectations of their expansive and ever growing clientele.

If you are new to the area or visiting and need to make a unique expression, thought or thank you to a special someone, the team at this long established shop will create the awe you want manifested.

Walk-in's are welcome, however free parking is limited and street slots are metered, so I'd suggest a combination of calling and Internet communication first.

Major credit cards accepted, along with regular and express delivery options are available.
